<div id="review_211905228" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/211905228" />
    <a title="Karen Ng" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/251567-karen-ng"><img alt="Karen Ng" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444188199p2/251567.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/211905228?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen Ng" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen Ng" href="/user/show/251567-karen-ng">Karen Ng</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/251567-karen-ng?shelf=thrill-ride">thrill-ride</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/251567-karen-ng?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer211905228" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8611257342986634534">This book deserves a 3.5 stars. As I said, as a long time Crichton fan, I probably came equipped with an overly high expectation. The book started out slow, with lots of loose ends that needed to be tied together, but came together nicely at around 30%. Without giving too much away, I'd have to say Crichton's high-tech, breakthrough technology is here, as well as the thrill factor, so the book is a page-turner. The general idea of the plot was good, and the story could be easily adapted into a m</span>
  <span id="freeText8611257342986634534" style="display:none">This book deserves a 3.5 stars. As I said, as a long time Crichton fan, I probably came equipped with an overly high expectation. The book started out slow, with lots of loose ends that needed to be tied together, but came together nicely at around 30%. Without giving too much away, I'd have to say Crichton's high-tech, breakthrough technology is here, as well as the thrill factor, so the book is a page-turner. The general idea of the plot was good, and the story could be easily adapted into a movie like all his other books.<br /><br />What I did not like about the book, is that the characters, especially the few graduate students, blur together a bit in the beginning. I had a hard time telling them apart, and I had no idea who the main characters were, until the very end; since once I developed the liking and understanding of one, she or he gets killed off. The villain is a bit too unrealistic and inhuman.<br /><br />Preston was good in given reliable and descriptive scientific facts throughout the book...but weak in story telling and character development. I was quite surprised about this since his non-fictions, "The Hot Zone", and "Demon in the Freezer" read almost like a great fictional story. However, for readers who thrive on facts, you would learn a lot about insects, plants, as well as toxins in this story. Overall, it was an enjoyable read, and I think all Crichton fans should read it, but wait for the price drop first.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8611257342986634534" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_752004305" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/752004305" />
    <a title="Mike Moore" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2644896-mike-moore"><img alt="Mike Moore" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/752004305?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike Moore" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike Moore" href="/user/show/2644896-mike-moore">Mike Moore</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780060873172" href="/book/show/13623736-micro">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer752004305" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18227377265127030078">You might think that my low rating indicates that I didn't like this book. This is not so, it's just that "ratings" or even "words" are an insufficient mode of expression to describe the experience of this, Crichton's last novel. No, to truly understand the sense of wonder, incredulity really, that this book inspires, a more subtle form is required. I'll go further: while many of MCs other books lend themselves to reinterpretation as B movies, Micro would probably be best experienced as an inter</span>
  <span id="freeText18227377265127030078" style="display:none">You might think that my low rating indicates that I didn't like this book. This is not so, it's just that "ratings" or even "words" are an insufficient mode of expression to describe the experience of this, Crichton's last novel. No, to truly understand the sense of wonder, incredulity really, that this book inspires, a more subtle form is required. I'll go further: while many of MCs other books lend themselves to reinterpretation as B movies, Micro would probably be best experienced as an interpretive dance. I can imagine it as consisting of the following movements:<br /><br />Introduction (The Sophomoric PhD students enter the world of high tech business ventures)<br />Behold! My Shrink Ray!<br />Snake!<br />I’m an evil man with a nefarious plan<br />(Even at one inch tall) We're students first<br />Ants!<br />Centipede!<br />Spiders!<br />Birds!<br />Wasps!<br />Bats!<br />The evil that men do (Oh, the betrayal!)<br />I’m an evil man with a nefarious plan (reprise)<br />Only I can control my evil robots<br />I cannot control my evil robots<br />All our friends are dead (Happy Ending)<br /><br /><br />In summary, while this may be appallingly bad as a "book", it can be considered quite positively as a blueprint for some form of commercially oriented performance art. <br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="18227377265127030078" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24175715?shelf=on-my-kindle">on-my-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24175715?shelf=thrillling-thrillers">thrillling-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24175715?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1821734448" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer640574660092382942">Frankly, it was not what I was looking for from Crichton. Nevertheless, a good read.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15405734849629651985">Nano-techno thriller - fun at times, but pretty frightening mostly<br/><br/>Kudos to Richard Preston, who had the daunting task of completing the inimitable Michael Crichton's last work. <br/><br/>It's Honey I Shrunk the Kids with real bad guys, and it gets frightening at times. But if you're a Crichton fan or anyone else, give this one a shot.</span>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/240208897" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/240208897?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew" href="/user/show/800291-andrew">Andrew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007350001" href="/book/show/13604348-micro">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer240208897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8093516575642898612">Ok I will put my hand up to this one - I really enjoyed it - ok I know that Crichton has fallen from favour in recent years and yes I read Pirates Latitude and was rather disappointed - especially since On Stranger Tides was being released (and I loved the book not the film - bit thats a rant for another day) anyway lets say that I remember reading Jurassic park all those years ago - and I loved it (the film I did too apart from lots of screaming children who do not do what they are told to do -</span>
  <span id="freeText8093516575642898612" style="display:none">Ok I will put my hand up to this one - I really enjoyed it - ok I know that Crichton has fallen from favour in recent years and yes I read Pirates Latitude and was rather disappointed - especially since On Stranger Tides was being released (and I loved the book not the film - bit thats a rant for another day) anyway lets say that I remember reading Jurassic park all those years ago - and I loved it (the film I did too apart from lots of screaming children who do not do what they are told to do - ok rant two for another day) - but this book i really enjoyed - it had it all - suspense, horror - twists and turns. I read the last 1/4 of the book in a day I enjoyed it that much - now do not think your getting his best work -no but you are getting some of his best - there were many plot twists you could see a mile off - and others I will admit caught me out - but that is how it should be I think. Either way I enjoyed it and was surprised I did so much - Its just a shame that this is effectively his swan song but still I can think of worse books to be remembered by. For me I will read this one again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8093516575642898612" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_346328318" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/346328318" />
    <a title="Sue" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/243372-sue"><img alt="Sue" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421897385p2/243372.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/346328318?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sue" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sue" href="/user/show/243372-sue">Sue</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/243372-sue?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer346328318" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11170257155199541501">This is the Michael Crichton I came to love in Jurassic Park. An adventure book filled with information and real science, and description to keep me turning the pages til I got to the end. I could not put this one down! The story centers on a company in Hawaii called Nanigen who is involved in drug research. Only they have a what can only be described as a rogue CEO who is greedier and more evil than the worst you can think of. When 7 college students come to Hawaii at the company's invitation V</span>
  <span id="freeText11170257155199541501" style="display:none">This is the Michael Crichton I came to love in Jurassic Park. An adventure book filled with information and real science, and description to keep me turning the pages til I got to the end. I could not put this one down! The story centers on a company in Hawaii called Nanigen who is involved in drug research. Only they have a what can only be described as a rogue CEO who is greedier and more evil than the worst you can think of. When 7 college students come to Hawaii at the company's invitation Vin Drake, CEO, promptly minaturizes them and sends them into the jungle hoping to get rid of them so he can cover up a murder. The insects, and microbes they encounter and the wit with which they survive is what makes this book intensly fast moving. The story moves through some predicitable spots with characters being killed off by giant spiders, drowned in downpours of rain, and fending off armed assasins that have also been inserted into the miniature world, but the ending is truly Michael Crichton! It's a surprise and it leaves no doubt that we'll see this one on the big screen.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11170257155199541501" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Se5b+dqSdbbN9OiNhHykAegx9BM18d7c9b8f9p9aXTWVgueGkhLkQwJX2ebmXIytdcQptfHdyU9dBI/qnuE9tA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/B4Di6WmPZSjP1Z0Vq9zfVtL4Y78QysR3Rw9VpW80+Agcr/07SasYWycZx80j1vRxr48KDhvPIJ1p61KlAezYQ==')})
  }

In The Demon in the Freezer, his first nonfiction book since The Hot Zone, a #1 New York Times bestseller, Richard Preston takes us into the heart of Usamriid, the United States Army Medical Research Institute of Infectious Diseases at Fort Detrick, Maryland, once the headquarters of the U.S. biological weapons program and now the epicenter of national biodefense.Peter Jahrling, the top scientist at Usamriid, a wry virologist who cut his teeth on Ebola, one of the world’s most lethal emerging viruses, has ORCON security clearance that gives him access to top secret information on bioweapons. His most urgent priority is to develop a drug that will take on smallpox-and win. Eradicated from the planet in 1979 in one of the great triumphs of modern science, the smallpox virus now resides, officially, in only two high-security freezers-at the Centers for Disease Control in Atlanta and in Siberia, at a Russian virology institute called Vector. But the demon in the freezer has been set loose. It is almost certain that illegal stocks are in the possession of hostile states, including Iraq and North Korea. Jahrling is haunted by the thought that biologists in secret labs are using genetic engineering to create a new superpox virus, a smallpox resistant to all vaccines.Usamriid went into a state of Delta Alert on September 11 and activated its emergency response teams when the first anthrax letters were opened in New York and Washington, D.C. Preston reports, in unprecedented detail, on the government’s response to the attacks and takes us into the ongoing FBI investigation.           if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/5194.Michael_Crichton">About Michael Crichton</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/5194.Michael_Crichton"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1359042651p3/5194.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/5194.Michael_Crichton">Michael Crichton
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
13,858
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2430793589581876916">Michael Crichton (1942-2008) was one of the most successful novelists of his generation, admired for his meticulous scientific research and fast-paced narrative. He graduated summa cum laude and earned his MD from Harvard Medical School in 1969. His first novel, <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18078737.Odds_On' title='Odds On' rel='nofollow noopener'>Odds On</a>
</i> (1966), was written under the pseudonym <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12619.John_Lange' title='John Lange' rel='nofollow noopener'>John Lange</a> and was followed by seven more Lange novels. He also wrote as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/85503.Michael_Douglas' title='Michael Douglas' rel='nofollow noopener'>Michael Doug</a></span>
  <span id="freeText2430793589581876916" style="display:none">Michael Crichton (1942-2008) was one of the most successful novelists of his generation, admired for his meticulous scientific research and fast-paced narrative. He graduated summa cum laude and earned his MD from Harvard Medical School in 1969. His first novel, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18078737.Odds_On" title="Odds On" rel="nofollow noopener">Odds On</a>
</i> (1966), was written under the pseudonym <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12619.John_Lange" title="John Lange" rel="nofollow noopener">John Lange</a> and was followed by seven more Lange novels. He also wrote as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/85503.Michael_Douglas" title="Michael Douglas" rel="nofollow noopener">Michael Douglas</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/607284.Jeffery_Hudson" title="Jeffery Hudson" rel="nofollow noopener">Jeffery Hudson</a>. His novel <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7663.A_Case_of_Need" title="A Case of Need" rel="nofollow noopener">A Case of Need</a>
</i> won the Edgar Award in 1969. Popular throughout the world, he has sold more than 200 million books. His novels have been translated into thirty-eight languages, and thirteen have been made into films.<br /><br />Michael Crichton passed away from lymphoma in 2008. He was 66 years old.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2430793589581876916" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

It’s unforgiving, uninterested. If you live or die, succeed or fail, feel pleasure or pain, it doesn’t care. That’s intolerable to us. How can we live in a world so indifferent to us. So we redefine nature. We call it Mother Nature when it’s not a parent in any real sense of the term.&rdquo;</span>
